Meetings of Various Circles to Promote the National Calendar for the New Year 96

The plan to promote the National Calendar for the New Year in this city has been discussed by various circles convened by the Social Affairs Bureau. The previous report has been noted. Yesterday afternoon, the second meeting was held at the Social Affairs Bureau. More than 20 representatives attended, including Chen Guangcheng from the City Government, Zhang Yaoming from the City Party Department, Zheng Chengqing from the City Chamber of Commerce, and representatives from various bureaus of the City Government. Chairman Feng Liutang presided over the ceremony. The detailed plan for promoting the National Calendar for the New Year and eliminating the Lunar Calendar for the New Year has been drafted in detail, and the principles have all been adopted. The implementation plan will be decided at the next meeting and will then be submitted to the City Government for promulgation. The drafted plan is recorded below:

Regarding New Year Customs (1) House Cleaning Reform Method: In accordance with the central government's regulations on garbage removal, all houses and household items should be cleaned thoroughly on December 15th. Enforcement measures: Those who do not perform the cleaning will be executed by people on their behalf in accordance with Article 7 of the regulations, and fees will be charged and penalties will be imposed in accordance with Article 9. (2) Sending off the Stove God and Welcoming the Stove God Reform Method: The practice of sending off the Stove God on the 23rd and 24th of the Lunar Calendar in the past, and welcoming the Stove God on New Year's Eve and the second night of the New Year, will be changed to the same dates on the National Calendar. Enforcement measures: Selling Stove God sedan chairs in the 12th month of the Lunar Calendar will be confiscated and a fine will be imposed. Pedestrians carrying them will be confiscated by the police on duty at any time, and rewards will be given based on the number of confiscations. If residents violate this, in addition to confiscating their incense, candles, and paper horses, the head of the household may be subject to appropriate punishment. The best method of punishment is to order the police to take them to the surrounding areas to publicize the ban. (3) Wax Offering (Thanksgiving) Reform Method: The practice of holding thanksgiving ceremonies in the 12th month of the Lunar Calendar, using paper foil, incense candles, fish, meat, and livestock, and setting off firecrackers must be changed to be held in the 12th month of the National Calendar this year. Enforcement measures: Selling thanksgiving items is prohibited at the end of the Lunar Calendar, and the district offices will notify people in advance. (1) Absolutely prohibit the setting off of firecrackers, sparklers, shooting stars, and other items from February 1st. Violators will be detained and fined. (2) If, during the Lunar New Year, a resident is fined, the housewife will be fined; if a business is fined, the manager will be fined. The disposal of the fines is the same as above. (4) Ancestral Worship, New Year's Eve Dinner, and Spring Banquet should all be changed to be held at the end and beginning of the National Calendar year. (5) New Year Greetings Reform Method: Changed to be held from January 1st to 5th. Enforcement Measures: (1) Please ask the Postal and Telegraph Bureau to prohibit the sending of Lunar New Year greeting telegrams and publish a notice in the newspaper in early December. (2) No stores are allowed to display or sell New Year's cards. (3) No New Year advertisements are allowed to be published. (6) Spring Couplets Reform Method: Changed to be sold at the end of the National Calendar year and pasted for the New Year. Enforcement Measures: Those who sell spring couplets at the end of the Lunar Calendar will have them confiscated and be sentenced to one day of detention. (7) Opening Market Day and Respecting the God of Wealth Reform Method: Changed to be held on the evening of January 4th. The 5th will be designated as the Five Roads Day for opening the market. Enforcement Measures: If it is held at the beginning of the Lunar New Year, police officers may enter and confiscate all items used for worshiping the gods and impose a small punishment. (8) Burning New Year Incense Reform Method: Allowed to be held from dawn one day later until the 15th. Enforcement Measures: Temples are not allowed to be opened on the thirtieth night of the Lunar Calendar and will be stopped by police officers. (9) Celebrating the Lantern Festival Reform Method: Scheduled to be held on January 15th. Enforcement Measures: No New Year gongs and drums or parades are allowed on the Lunar New Year's Day, and no flower lanterns are allowed to be sold during the Lunar New Year period. Violators will have their flower lanterns, gongs, and drums confiscated.

Regarding Industry and Commerce (1) Account Closing Reform Method: Comply with Executive Yuan Order No. 3987 to hold at the end of the year. Enforcement Measures: If the people do not clear accounts at the end of the National Calendar year, stores may charge interest for the extension. Merchants who do not collect accounts at the end of the National Calendar year may allow debtors to pay in the first accounting period of the following year. (2) New Year Holiday Reform Method: Changed to be held from January 1st to 4th. Those whose original customary holidays exceed this number may move them to the end and beginning of the National Calendar year in comparison (such as the opening of the dyeing industry, the green cylinder industry, and the grain industry). Enforcement Measures: (1) It is strictly forbidden to suspend business at the beginning and end of the Lunar Calendar year under the pretext of the Spring Festival or other names. Violators will be ordered to open for business by the police station and the store owner or manager will be fined. (2) Trade associations, etc., will be sanctioned by party and government agencies. The measures will be determined and promulgated by party and government agencies. (3) If stores and factories take holidays at the beginning of the Lunar Calendar year, even if it is stopped, if the initiative comes from the capital side, the salaries of shop assistants and workers will be doubled per day; if it comes from the shop assistants and workers, their salaries will also be doubled per day. A joint announcement will be made by the City Party Department and the Social Affairs Bureau. (3) Reform Methods for Game Venues and Restaurants: All theater closures and repair closures for game venues and restaurants are allowed to be carried out at the end of the National Calendar year, but they should all be open for business by the New Year to provide entertainment for the public. Enforcement Measures: Violators will be punished in accordance with the preceding items. (4) Double Salary and Bonus: Double salaries and annual bonuses should also be changed to be paid in accordance with the National Calendar.

Regarding Education (1) Reform Method for Classes at the End and Beginning of the Lunar Calendar Year: Enforcement Measures: The Education Bureau will select staff to conduct a strict investigation of each school during this period. Violators will be punished.

Regarding Trade Unions (1) In accordance with the central government's notice, publicize the method of promoting the National Calendar for the New Year to workers as much as possible. (2) Notify all workers that they must not ask the capital side to stop work and give leave at the end and beginning of the Lunar Calendar year. Violators will be expelled from their membership and the capital side will double their wages. (3) If factories condone or are not enthusiastic about promoting the National Calendar for the New Year, the City Party Department and the Civil Training Committee will punish them. The punishment method will be formulated and announced by the Civil Training Committee.

Regarding the Chamber of Commerce (1) Should assist the government in promoting the National Calendar for the New Year as much as possible and fully implement government orders. (2) Immediately convene various trade associations to state the significance of promoting the National Calendar for the New Year and abolishing the Lunar New Year, and forward it to various businesses for publicity and compliance.

Regarding the News Industry (1) Disclose the texts and news of the promotion of the National Calendar for the New Year as much as possible. (2) Regarding the significance of promoting the National Calendar for the New Year and abolishing the Lunar Calendar, reporters should write words, books, and pictures to promote it widely. (3) Each newspaper should suspend publication for one week at the end of the year. This year, it should suspend publication on December 26th of the National Calendar and resume publication on January 4th of the following year. (4) At the beginning and end of the Lunar Calendar year, printing unions and newspaper delivery unions must not stop work. The City Party Department and the Civil Training Committee should notify each union in advance to comply. (5) No New Year's advertisements are allowed to be published at the beginning of the Lunar Calendar year.

Regarding Party and Government Agencies (1) In addition to carrying out the above-mentioned affairs in their respective capacities, all party and government personnel should set an example and must not have any violations. Those who violate this will be punished according to their discipline. (2) The Propaganda Department of the City Party Department should supervise its subordinate district branches to vigorously promote the promotion of the National Calendar for the New Year to the people, such as open-air speeches and printing and distributing slogans and propaganda materials in simple vernacular words and pictures. (3) Party and government personnel are not allowed to ask for leave from February 10th to the end of February unless they have an illness or important matter and have proof. (4) Each agency's New Year holiday is only three days including commemorative days. At the beginning of the promotion, may the City Government be requested to forward it to the National Government to allow a holiday from December 30th to January 4th to attract social attention and promote the concept of valuing the National Calendar. Moreover, for the sake of closing accounts, civil servants cannot be without family affairs to deal with. The length of this holiday at the end and beginning of the year should be appropriately extended. (5) Party and government agencies, together with various groups, should organize a survey team to abolish the rituals of the old Lunar New Year and assign segments to be responsible for visiting and investigating. If there are still situations in which Thanksgiving ceremonies, business suspensions, and respect for the God of Wealth are held around the Lunar New Year, a disciplinary punishment will be given in terms of reputation. After inviting the police on duty to provide evidence, a warning should be posted on the door, stating words such as "Private Lunar New Year ritual celebrations should be strictly prohibited" or "Stubbornly adhering to Lunar Calendar ideology is outdated," so as to serve as a warning. If they disregard the posting, a note should be written stating that they will comply with the National Calendar in the future, signed by the head of the household, and submitted to the survey team for filing.

Regarding General Publicity (1) The methods for promoting the National Calendar for the New Year should be simply printed in the form of leaflets, about 400,000 copies, which will be printed by the Fifth Section of the City Government and handed over to the Public Security Bureau in each district for distribution to households from the 20th of this month to the end of the month, so that every household knows and has time to prepare. (2) Compile simple lyrics and folk songs to promote the National Calendar, and have students from city schools perform them in different locations. (3) Each group should give public speeches or dress-up performances, or write words and sentences to be shown in each theater. (4) During the National Calendar New Year period, organize cheering teams such as New Year gongs and drums, dragon lanterns, etc., or firecracker teams to set off firecrackers to create a New Year atmosphere. (5) Set a period as the National Calendar Promotion Memorial Week, unite people from all walks of life to hold a large parade. The parade route must be widespread, and please ask each newspaper to use a special column to publicize as much as possible and hold entertainment events, etc., or set the two weeks before and after the National Calendar New Year as Publicity Week. (6) Or have each group and public institution purchase fireworks and choose a place to set them off, or hold a lantern festival, etc.

Regarding Celebration Rituals (1) New Year Family Rituals (A) New Year's Eve is a memorial for ancestors. Gather family members, young and old, to offer incense and flowers and hang portraits of ancestors in the central hall. The memorial ceremony is as follows: (1) Stand at attention (2) Pay respects to the ancestors (3) The head of the family offers incense and flowers (4) Explain the meaning of the commemoration, so that they know the gains and experiences of the past year, and instruct them on the legacy and anecdotes of the ancestors, which are sufficient to serve as admonitions. (5) The younger generation pays New Year's greetings to the elders (6) Family feast (7) New Year's Day Celebration Rituals (A) Stand at attention (B) Pay respects to the national flag (C) Pay respects to the ancestors (D) The head of the family explains the meaning of the New Year celebration, so that they are aware of the efforts to begin the New Year with learning and career, and encourages family members (E) The younger generation pays New Year's greetings to the elders and relatives (F) The head of the family bestows financial rewards, food, and cultural items to the younger generation (G) Banquet (H) Entertainment

Prohibition of Spring Festival Holiday 97

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has instructed the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to investigate and prevent reported resolutions by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Bankers' Association to designate February 17th and 18th as a two-day holiday for all industries during the Spring Festival. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, citing that the resolution contradicts Article 1 of the Central Executive Committee's regulations promoting the adoption of the Gregorian calendar, suspects the report is inaccurate. It has ordered the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to investigate and prevent this. The official order is recorded below:

Order to comply: It is hereby noted that according to today's newspaper, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Bankers' Association have resolved to abolish the lunar calendar in accordance with the National Government's order, designating February 17th and 18th as a two-day Spring Festival holiday, and January 1st to 3rd as the New Year holiday, along with Sunday the 4th, for a total of four days. In order to facilitate coordination, foreign banks have also decided to follow this arrangement for both the Gregorian calendar and abolished lunar New Year holidays. However, Article 1 of the Central Executive Committee's regulations promoting the adoption of the Gregorian calendar stipulates that the holiday dates and various rituals and entertainment associated with the abolished lunar New Year should be moved to around the Gregorian calendar New Year, and that no holidays are permitted during the abolished lunar New Year, nor may holidays be taken under other pretexts. This has been ordered by the Executive Yuan to all provincial and municipal governments for compliance, and this bureau has relayed the order for compliance and jointly announced it with the Municipal Party Department and the Public Safety Bureau, requiring all citizens to comply. The name "Spring Festival" has long been eliminated, and it is not included in the Central Government's designated commemorative events. If February 17th and 18th are arbitrarily designated as a Spring Festival holiday, it would inevitably perpetuate the use of the abolished lunar calendar and hinder the promotion of the Gregorian calendar. It must be understood that Shanghai is the focus of attention for the national business community, and the Chamber of Commerce is the leader of the commercial groups, and the Bankers' Association is the model for all industries. It is unlikely that they would deliberately violate government orders. This bureau sincerely hopes that the newspaper report is not factual, so as not to damage the reputation of the association. However, since it has been reported, you are instructed to investigate, send a letter to correct the report, so as to avoid confusion, and notify the business community to prepare for year-end closing of accounts and New Year's customs and rituals as early as possible, so that they are held at the end of this Gregorian calendar year and the coming New Year, and not continue to follow the abolished lunar calendar. This is of utmost importance. This order is issued.

Wang Yansong Reports on the Progress of the Industry and Commerce Conference 98

Industry regulations case handed over to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for adoption and implementation. Closing accounts and collecting debts are two separate issues. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce held a weekly memorial service for Dr. Sun Yat-sen yesterday and invited Standing Committee Member Wang Yansong to report on the progress of the Industry and Commerce Conference and important issues such as industry regulations, Gregorian calendar closing of accounts, etc. More than 240 representatives from over 50 industry associations and 51 members of the Chamber of Commerce staff attended. Chairman Cheng Bian presided over the ceremony. After Secretary-General Ru Chengqing reported on important meetings of the past week, Standing Committee Member Wang Yansong gave a report, stating that the purpose of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce convening the Industry and Commerce Conference was to vigorously implement the Party's industry and commerce policies, promote the development of national production, increase foreign trade, and enhance the national economy. It was hoped to gather the talents and abilities of officials and businessmen from across the country and collect the benefits of diverse opinions. Therefore, the participants in this conference included representatives serving in industry and commerce administrative agencies, leaders of the business community, experts studying economic theories, and representatives from as far as Sichuan, Guangdong, Liaoning, Ningxia, and overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia, all gathered together. The number of proposals was numerous. Not counting the temporary motions, there were a total of 406 proposals. If these 406 proposals had to be discussed one by one, even if the Industry and Commerce Conference was extended from eight days to one or two months, it would still be difficult to achieve. Therefore, after receiving the proposals, six review committees were organized to sort, classify, analyze, and study the proposals according to their nature. The first group reviewed matters concerning industry and commerce policies and administrative regulations. The second group reviewed matters concerning international trade and transportation. The third group reviewed matters concerning labor, labor disputes, and scientific management. The fourth group reviewed matters concerning industry and commerce finance and taxation. The fifth group reviewed matters concerning the development of industry and promotion, protection, and improvement of domestic goods. The sixth group reviewed matters concerning national unemployment and industry and commerce relief and other matters. After each group reviewed the proposals and drafted a review report, it was submitted to the conference for discussion. The results of the conference discussions can be divided into ten categories: (1) matters concerning resisting economic aggression; (2) matters concerning joint operations; (3) matters concerning reorganizing tariff regulations; (4) matters concerning improving the currency system; (5) matters concerning scientific management methods and industrial rationalization; (6) matters concerning basic industries; (7) matters concerning indigenous industries; (8) matters concerning labor welfare; (9) matters concerning unemployment issues; and (10) matters concerning international trade. Each of the above ten categories had resolutions passed. A detailed report is not possible due to time constraints. Therefore, I will only report on the four issues that are of most concern to the various industries: (1) implementing methods of labor-management cooperation. This proposal was submitted by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce and was passed in its original form after the first review. However, when it was submitted to the conference, members paid close attention, and detailed and thorough statements were made by all parties. As a result of the discussion, it was returned to the review committee. After the second review, the phrase "the management rights of the factory are the inherent rights of the factory" was added, and other amendments were made to the original proposal before it was passed by the conference. (2) The case of industries complying with industry regulations. The proposal that industries should uniformly comply with industry regulations approved by the competent authorities was proposed by Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, and was the issue of greatest concern to the various industry associations in this city. According to the nature of this proposal, it should have belonged to the first review. The result of the review was "submitted to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for reference." After being submitted to the conference, the Shanghai industry and commerce representatives present believed that this case had previously been approved by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, and if it was still submitted to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for reference, there would inevitably be little result. Therefore, they unanimously opposed it and explained the reasons in detail. As a result of the discussion, it was returned to the review committee. The result of the second review was "requesting the Judicial Yuan to interpret it." When it was submitted to the conference, the situation was very tense because it was already the sixth day of the conference, and many of the industry and commerce representatives from Shanghai and other places had already left Beijing. Therefore, there were fewer people speaking for the business community. In addition, representatives serving in industry and commerce administrative agencies inevitably expressed sympathy for the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's position. Economic and legal experts, on the one hand, were not familiar with business conditions and customs, and on the other hand, felt that the case had no legal basis and did not generate legal interest, so they felt indifferent to the case. But since the situation at the meeting was such, and we remembered the earnest expectations and heavy trust of the various industries, if the case had no results, we would have no way to face all the industries in the city. Therefore, we had to work hard to persevere. It was estimated that the Judicial Yuan's interpretation was limited to laws that had such clauses but the meaning was not very clear. Since there was no such legal text in this case, it could not be requested for interpretation. Those with legal texts should follow the legal texts, and those without legal texts should follow customs. This is a principle recognized by legal scholars. If the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce receives a letter from the court requesting an investigation of customs, the court will also rely on the Chamber of Commerce's investigation and response as the basis for its judgment. It can be seen that customs has its own strong position in law. Now that there are thousands of years of customary law for industries to comply with industry regulations, and there is no explicit provision in the law, it should be handled in accordance with customs. After we stated this opinion, the atmosphere at the meeting changed. Unexpectedly, a representative from Northeast China proposed that the case of industries complying with industry regulations could not be implemented in the north, otherwise the industry associations would be suspected of manipulation and oppression. At that time, I also explained in detail the organizational laws of industry associations and chambers of commerce, saying that the staff of the associations are elected by the industries, and the staff of the chambers of commerce are elected by the industry associations. Since the industries trust them when they are elected, they can be removed according to law after they are elected. How can there be manipulation and oppression? Moreover, the industry regulations that industries should comply with are limited to those approved by the government, so the government is responsible for supervision and review, and there is no need to worry about manipulation and oppression. At that time, the original proposer, Director Pan Gongzhan, also gave a very detailed explanation, saying that if there are no industry regulations that industries should comply with, the industry associations will inevitably disintegrate, and the foundation of the Chamber of Commerce will be shaken. If members of industry associations have to pay membership fees and raise public bonds at any time, and the industry regulations do not have to be complied with, then members only have obligations and no rights. Why should there be such industry associations? Not only this, but if the industry regulations do not have to be complied with, the financial market will inevitably be chaotic. For example, if the business hours of the money industry and the silver market are as standardized, what will be the impact on society? At that time, the members at the meeting suddenly realized after this explanation. As a result of the discussion, it was decided to "hand it over to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for adoption and implementation." It cannot be said that this result in the Industry and Commerce Conference was not due to the representatives' hard work. However, it is hoped that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce will be able to comply with commercial sentiment, respect the resolutions, and promptly adopt and implement them, so that the industry can be protected. (3) Gregorian calendar closing date. This proposal was submitted for discussion by the chambers of commerce of various counties in Jiangsu. Minister Kong happened to be the chairman at the time. Minister Kong made some explanations on this proposal, saying that the government has the determination to follow the Gregorian calendar, and it may be difficult to request a change. However, this seat believes that closing accounts is one issue, and collecting debts is another issue. It is not necessary to collect debts after closing accounts. In the future, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce may issue an order stating that the business community should close accounts at the end of the Gregorian calendar year, but collecting debts can be done at the end of January or the end of February. In this way, those who pay the bills will not be able to use it as an excuse to delay, and there will be no violation of national government orders or business conditions. Since the members of the conference did not discuss the chairman's report, the proposal had no results or resolutions. (4) The case of joint operation with joint liability. The Civil Law regulates that joint operation with joint liability occurs suddenly. It is requested that supplementary clauses be discussed and approved and transferred to the Legislative Yuan for supplementary relief. This case was proposed by the Sichuan representative. After the representative's explanation, the members of the conference believed that it was worth discussing. As a result of the discussion, it was decided to "ask the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to draft measures and submit them to the Legislative Yuan for adoption." The above four cases are reported because they are closely related to the business community and are not afraid of being tedious. However, since the nature of the Industry and Commerce Conference is not a legally established power organ, the resolutions must be effectively adopted and implemented by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce in order to achieve the effectiveness of the conference. Therefore, in the future, on the one hand, it is hoped that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce will effectively implement them, and on the other hand, it is hoped that all members will not consider the meeting as a closed matter, but should continue to supervise and promote them at any time, so that this meeting will not be in vain. Finally, I hope that the government can effectively (1) abolish excessive taxes and miscellaneous fees; (2) eliminate bandits and communists in various places; (3) reorganize land and water transportation; and (4) accumulate capital, then the prosperity of industry and commerce can be expected.

Record of the Collision of the Xinfeng Steamer 99

The Keizan Maru failed to follow the navigation rules. The upper deck of the Xinfeng was destroyed. It returned to Shanghai for major repairs that day. It is not uncommon for Japanese ships to cause trouble. This time, the Xinfeng, a regular North China steamer of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, was damaged by a Japanese ship again on its way from Shanghai to Tianjin, causing huge losses. The details of this incident are recorded separately below:

The Truth About the Japanese Ship Causing the Trouble. The Xinfeng steamer of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company arrived at about 6:00 AM on the 9th, about two nautical miles from the Tanggu estuary. The ship was entering the Baihe River, and the Keizan Maru, a Kobe-Tianjin steamer of the Nippon Yusen Kaisha, was leaving Tianjin. The sea surface in that area is narrow, and the water level has been reduced recently. According to the rules, the Keizan Maru should have steered outward. Unexpectedly, the Japanese did not follow the navigation regulations and drove straight towards the Xinfeng steamer in the fairway. When the two ships were close to each other, Ma Xun, the captain of the Xinfeng, saw the Japanese ship coming head-on, and quickly pulled the siren to urge it to avoid to the outside. But the Japanese ship turned a deaf ear. In an instant, the two ships were close, and even if the Xinfeng urgently gave way, it was too late. With a bang, the Japanese ship crashed into the Xinfeng, and a great disaster was caused.

The Xinfeng Suffered Great Damage. The Japanese ship Keizan Maru has a displacement of about 4,000 tons, a huge hull, and a fast speed. If it had collided head-on, the Xinfeng would have sunk. Fortunately, the Xinfeng reversed to avoid the collision. However, the second and third decks of the ship were hit by the bow of the Keizan Maru, and the cabins and passenger rooms on these two decks, as well as the structures on the upper deck, were completely destroyed. Even the lifeboats on the deck were destroyed. Most of the second and third decks of the Xinfeng were destroyed. It can be seen that the loss was huge. If the passengers had not escaped early, a major tragedy would have occurred.

The Japanese Ship Admitted Its Fault. After the incident, Ma Xun, the captain of the Xinfeng, inspected the damage and negotiated with the captain of the Keizan Maru. Yesterday, the Shanghai Bureau received a telegram from Captain Ma Xun in Tianjin, stating that he had personally inspected the damaged area with the captain of the Japanese ship, drawn a diagram, and prepared it as the basis for negotiation. The Japanese knew that they were in the wrong. The captain of the Keizan Maru signed a document acknowledging the accident and taking responsibility. The document was received by Captain Ma Xun.

The Xinfeng Arrived in Tianjin to Unload Cargo. After inspecting the damage, the Xinfeng steamer was still able to sail because the cargo hold had not been damaged. Under the guidance of the pilot, it sailed into the Tianjin Zizhu Forest Wharf and docked. The passengers on board were only startled and not injured. They are now safely ashore. The cargo in the various holds is also being unloaded without any damage.

It Can Leave Tianjin Today. Because most of the passenger decks on the second and third floors have been destroyed, it is difficult to sail without major repairs in a dock. The ship is scheduled to leave Tianjin for Shanghai today. Yesterday, the Shanghai Bureau continued to receive telegrams from Tianjin saying that the Xinfeng steamer is still loading cargo from Tianjin as usual, but passengers are not being carried. The captain has ordered the business director to stop selling tickets for the sake of safe navigation. The amount of the loss will not be known until the ship arrives in Shanghai. Regarding the negotiations and claims against the Japanese ship, the Shanghai Bureau must also wait for the Xinfeng to arrive to inquire about the cause and course of the accident before the shipping department can estimate the loss and proceed with the claim.

Detailed Record of the Naval Second Fleet Maneuvers 100

More than ten warships, including the Chuyu, concentrated on Baguazhou in Nanjing for maneuvers. Under the command of Chen Shaokuan, Acting Minister of the Navy, the exercises have been going on for two weeks and will come to an end on the 5th of this month. It is said that on the 6th, Chen Shaokuan personally led the Chuyu, Jiangzhen, Chuqian, Jiangyuan, Chuguan, Chutai, and other ships of the Second Fleet from Beijing to the waters off Wusongkou for large-scale maneuvers. The ships were ordered to depart at 1:00 PM that afternoon. Chen personally led the entire Second Fleet staff on the flagship Chuyu to command, and summoned more than ten Tongji midshipmen and assigned them to various ships to increase their experience. When the flagship departed, the Yingrui warship stationed in Nanjing fired a 15-gun salute to show respect, and the Chuyu also returned the salute. Then, the ships followed each other in a single line at a distance of 400 yards. The fleet of warships advancing through the waves was extremely spectacular. During the voyage, the ships carried out various offensive and defensive tactics according to the signal flags, and practiced aircraft shooting. At about 4:00 PM, they passed the Jinshan and Jiaoshan mountains in Zhenjiang, and at 6:00 PM, they arrived at Dantu. As dusk fell, the ships were ordered to anchor. At 8:00 PM, the entire army maneuvered searchlights, and the electric torches were as bright as day. The terrain on both sides was clearly visible. Then they practiced the army's communication signals. The lights flashed on and off, transmitting messages, which was also very interesting. At 5:00 AM on the 7th, the sea breeze was biting cold and the dawn had not yet broken. Chen Shaokuan personally went to the lookout to command everything. At 7:00 AM, all the soldiers routinely stowed their hammocks, washed the decks, and performed physical exercises. At 9:00 AM, they arrived at Jiangyin. The Hai Chou warship was stationed there and fired a salute to greet them. The Chuyu returned the salute. At 10:00 AM, Chen ordered the entire army to practice international communication flags, about a hundred words. In a short time, it was completed. The soldiers' training in flag signals was indeed very skilled. Chen was very satisfied. At 11:00 AM, they passed the Duanshan Port. In the distance, the Qing Tian surveying boat was engaged in surveying work. At 1:00 PM, they passed Tongzhou. At 2:00 PM, they ordered the ships to practice firefighting, and the fire hoses were immediately prepared to be extremely fast. At 3:00 PM, the ships maneuvered various artillery techniques. At 4:00 PM, the entire team passed Liuhe. At about 5:00 PM, they arrived at Wusongkou. After the ships were ordered to anchor, they summoned the captains of each ship to the Chuyu flagship to give instructions on various maneuvers. At 7:00 PM, the entire army practiced the army's communication signals. At 8:00 PM, they suddenly ordered the ships to practice extinguishing fires and deploy night battle equipment. All the soldiers were well-trained and moved quickly. It is said that in addition to the six ships, including the Chuyu, Chen Shaobao also telegraphed the Yongsheng and Yisheng ships stationed in Shanghai to go to the waters off Wusongkou for joint exercises. At dawn on the 8th, Chen Shaokuan led the Second Fleet staff officers and aides from the Chuyu to the Chuqian warship, and ordered the ships to form a single line at 5:30 AM in a single line at a distance of 400 yards towards the Wusongkou waters, and divided the Chuqian, Chuguan, Chuyu, Yongsheng into the first team, and the Jiangzhen, Chutai, Jiangyuan, Yisheng into the second team. Along the way, they practiced various ship formations. The ships were arranged in various formations according to Chen's signal flags, changing their direction and situation. At about 8:00 AM, the weather at sea was windy. The soldiers still risked practicing fog cannons to convey orders. Therefore, in the thick fog, the ships could still operate freely, and they would not lose their targets or isolate the ships from each other. Then the rain became heavier, and all the officers and soldiers were drenched. Therefore, Chen ordered the entire team to return to Yiwosha and anchor. In the afternoon, the ships were ordered to operate freely, while the soldiers of the Chuyu wore raincoats and braved the rain to practice sampans, showing even more spirit. On the morning of the 9th, the sky was cloudy and the fog was thick. Chen still led the eight ships, including the Chuqian, to venture into the waters off Wusong. He also took the opportunity to launch fog cannons. The ships were able to fire cannons at a set time to convey orders. At the same time, he ordered the entire army to divide into two teams, A and B, to maneuver various fleet formations. The weather was slightly better at noon, but the wind was stronger and the waves were rough, so the ships swayed abnormally. However, the sailors were well-trained and accustomed to the wind and waves and did not suffer at all. After several hours of maneuvering ship formations, the entire team was near Huaniao Island. It was about 5:00 PM, so they ordered the ships to return to Yiwosha. They did not arrive at Yiwosha until 11:00 PM. On the morning of the 10th, Chen summoned the captains of the ships to the Chuyu flagship for training and pointed out the achievements of this exercise. At 7:00 AM, the ships were ordered to depart. The Jiangzhen, Chuqian, Chuguan, Jiangyuan, Chutai, Yongsheng, and Yisheng all went straight to Gaochang Temple and stationed there. Chen led the Chuyu flagship to Wusongkou to meet Chairman Chiang. At noon, Chairman Chiang took the Lianjing warship from Ningbo to Song. The Chuyu raised the full flag and fired a 21-gun salute. Chen then accompanied Chairman Chiang ashore to Shanghai.

British Female Aviator to Fly to Shanghai Tomorrow 102

The British female aviator, Mrs. Bruce, will fly to Shanghai tomorrow. She is piloting a single-engine aircraft on a flight from London to Tokyo. She departed from London on September 25. Originally, she planned to fly to Tokyo in 11 days. However, after quickly flying over Europe, she encountered difficulties in the Persian Gulf. She was forced to land and was trapped by Arabs. The aircraft was also damaged. There had been no news of Mrs. Bruce's flight for several days. Later, with the help of nearby British people, she repaired the aircraft and flew to Hong Kong at 2:20 PM on the 9th of this month. She was originally scheduled to fly from Hong Kong to Xiamen yesterday, and fly to Shanghai today. According to news from the British Consulate in Shanghai, Mrs. Bruce has now changed her itinerary and will fly from Hong Kong to Fuzhou this morning, the 8th, and fly to Shanghai tomorrow. The British Consul-General, Bai Linan, has inquired about the time of her arrival in Shanghai tomorrow by radio from Mrs. Bruce. Mrs. Bruce was a well-known British automotive pioneer. She has only been trained in aviation for a few months.

Strictly Interrogating the Assassin of Zhao 103

Two interrogations have revealed several important accomplices. The handling agency will ask the Provincial Government to re-determine the killer of Zhao Tieqiao, former specialist of the China Merchants Bureau, Xia Shaoen. After County Public Security Bureau Chief Shen Jinghua personally went to Hefei to bring him back to Shanghai, he was detained at the County Public Security Bureau on the morning before yesterday. At about 10:00 AM that morning, he was interrogated by Bureau Chief Shen. The interrogation did not use severe interrogation methods, but only ordinary interrogation procedures. The suspect Xia Shaoen detailed the reasons and the beginning and end of the assassination of Zhao, and confessed several important accomplices. Finally, he stated that he was willing to sacrifice himself and had no fear. He was upright and regarded himself as a Jianghu hero. At 2:30 PM yesterday afternoon, Bureau Chief Shen interrogated him for the second time. The details he confessed were the same as the day before. At 3:30 PM, he was ordered to be returned to the patrol room on the west side of the lower floor and strictly guarded. Strangers were not allowed to visit and were not allowed to talk to others. The agency handling the suspect will report the situation to the Provincial Government, and the Provincial Government will designate the agency to handle the case and issue a decision. Xia's wife, Qian, left Shanghai in late last month and rushed to Hefei, her hometown, because she heard that the County Public Security Bureau had sent people to arrest him. Therefore, she rushed back to Anhui overnight to prepare to notify her husband Xia Shaoen to flee elsewhere to avoid arrest. However, when Xia's wife returned to Xiadian Village in the eastern township of Hefei, her husband had already been arrested for three days.

Murder on Railway Station Road 112

"Small Heart" stabbed five times, bleeding immediately and collapsing. Gu Xiaoxing, nicknamed "Small Heart," 34 years old, from Taizhou, currently residing at 32 Derun Lane, Railway Station Road, had paid homage to staff member Xu as his "Old Man." Gu had a close relationship with Cao Binglin, a gangster residing on Coal Dregs Road, and Cao had also paid homage to Mr. Pan, the owner of a local meat shop, as his "Old Man." Unexpectedly, Cao and Gu became estranged while helping friends, harboring private resentments. Suddenly, the other day, Cao, Gu, and others gathered to gamble at a house on Coal Dregs Road, and another argument broke out. Fortunately, the gamblers present persuaded them to disperse, preventing further incidents. However, yesterday at 8 a.m., Cao and Gu each summoned friends seeking revenge, and Cao Binglin made the first move, holding a sharp knife and waiting in Derun Lane. Gu Xiaoxing happened to be leaving his house to also invite friends, and they encountered each other. Cao Binglin then stabbed Gu violently with the knife, inflicting five wounds: two on the left shoulder, two on the right leg, and one fatal wound to the left waist. Gu immediately collapsed, bleeding profusely, and died instantly. The assailant, seeing that Gu was seriously injured and had collapsed, immediately fled. Subsequently, Chief Ma of the Second District Police Station on Railway Station Road learned of the incident and led police to investigate. They found that Gu had already died and the assailant had fled. The assailant's brother, Cao Bingsheng, was taken to the station for questioning, and then transferred to the Second District Headquarters and forwarded to the court for investigation. Meanwhile, the local bailiff was ordered to report to the court for an inquest. At 2 p.m., the court dispatched a prosecutor accompanied by an coroner to the scene for an inquest. It was confirmed that the deceased had been stabbed five times, with the one to the left waist being fatal. A coroner's report was filled out, and the family of the deceased was ordered to prepare a coffin for burial. A strict search for the fugitive Cao Binglin was ordered to bring him to justice.

Two Bandits Executed Yesterday 113

Yu BaoRen insists on preserving his face. Cao Jinbiao has nothing to say. Liu Nianchun, the owner of Dingkang Gold Shop on Ningbo Road, was kidnapped by bandits at the entrance of his residence on North Chengdu Road on July 5th of this year, at 6:15 p.m., and a ransom of 40,000 yuan was demanded. The case was solved by Chinese Detectives Cao Ashan and Ruan Yao of the New Gate Police Station. One of the kidnappers, Yu BaoRen (29 years old) from Wuxi, was sent to the Special District Court for interrogation and confessed to the crime. On September 4th, Judge Sun Yuan sentenced him to death, and the sentence was submitted to the provincial government for approval. Yesterday afternoon, at the appointed time, the police escorted Yu to the Second Criminal Court of the court, where Judge Cheng Shangfeng questioned Yu about any last words. According to Yu, he requested that a letter be sent to his father, Yu Xinwan, at 1629 Chun Gui Lane, Haining Road, asking him not to come to collect his body after the execution and not to grieve, as he was harmed by others and had no face to return the body to his hometown. If there were any remaining funds, he could hire monks to pray for him and arrange for his sister to find a husband, and his wife was still young and could remarry. He had nothing else to say. Judge Cheng ordered him to be sent to the local court for execution. Another bandit, Cao Jinbiao, led a gang armed with weapons to break into the residence of Gu Maodi on Changping Road in West Shanghai on the evening of March 31st, at 8 p.m., robbing 343 yuan of property and shooting and killing Chinese Constable Liu Youqing of No. 463, and committing other robberies. After the case was reported, Chinese Detective Shen Chongli of the Gordon Road Police Station and others arrested Cao and sent him to the Special District Local Court for interrogation and sentencing to death, which was reported to the provincial government for approval. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Cheng also came to the Second Criminal Court. According to Cao Jinbiao, he was from Jiangbei, 24 years old, and used to engage in kidnapping. He had a lined robe, glasses, a watch, silver coins, and change that were confiscated in the police station, and he requested that they be returned to his uncle, Wang Kui Cai, who lives at 7 Tianfu Lane, at the intersection of Hanzhong Road and Mingyuan Road in Binbei. He had nothing else to say and begged for food. Judge Cheng ordered him to be sent to the Local Court for execution and ordered Wang Kui Cai to be summoned to the court to receive the items. Then the Chinese and Western detectives led Yu and Cao down, along with photos and files, and escorted them in a car directly to the execution ground in Caohe. The Local Court appointed Prosecutor Yang Wenjun as the supervising officer and brought the court clerk and examiners, and ordered Police Chief Yang Deshan, Police Sergeant Chen Xihui, and Execution Police Gu Hanqing and Wang Jianqing, and assistant police Hu Xianglin, Cai Zuoqing, and Zhang Chunsen, six people in total, to rush to the execution ground. After the judge took his seat, he questioned Yu BaoRen, who stated that he was 29 years old, from Wuxi, and lived on Haining Road. His father's name was Yu Xinhuai, and he had a sworn brother named Tian Hongsheng. After his death, please notify his father and friends, but do not write that he was shot, just say he died of a sudden illness, because death is not strange, but face is important. Cao Jinbiao said that he was 24 years old, from Funing, and lived in Tianbao Lane, he had nothing to say. The official order was executed, and Police Chief Yang ordered the police to lead them down for execution. The bodies were collected by the hall for burial.

Hu Fuzhang's Mental Illness Problem 115

Hu held a knife with intent to kill his mother.

Was it a mental illness outbreak?

This point needs to be carefully identified.

The judge set a two-month deadline. Sun Kui, the preparing director of the Forensic Medical Examination Institute of the Judicial Administration Department, was previously reported to be going to France soon to purchase medical equipment. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Tingqi of the Special District Court continued the trial of Hu Fuzhang, the son of Hu Aji, a Chinese constable of the Three Docks Police Station in Hongkou, who held a knife with intent to kill his mother. Sun specially came to court to testify. After Hu Fuzhang was accused, his father and uncle both testified that Fuzhang had a mental illness. The court ordered Sun Da Fang to examine him. According to Sun's report, he was indeed suffering from mental illness. Subsequently, the HSBC Police Station sent Hu Fuzhang to the Public Works Department Hospital for examination. After the hospital kept Hu for seven days and was repeatedly diagnosed by Western doctors, no mental illness was found. They reported to the court that he was free of mental illness. Judge Wu reviewed the reports of the forensic doctor and the Public Works Department doctor, which were completely contradictory. It was difficult to determine which was correct. The case was postponed pending further investigation. The above was reported previously. Yesterday morning, in addition to Sun's testimony, a Chinese doctor surnamed Huang from the Public Works Department Hospital also came to court to state the diagnosis of Hu Fuzhang's condition. Judge Wu first asked Hu Aji if the defendant had a mental illness. According to Aji, my son Fuzhang had his head broken by a teacher with a ruler when he was studying at Tianbao Lane, and blood flowed like a waterfall. He was sent to the hospital for treatment, and because the teacher had apologized, he was still allowed to study with him. He only suffered from mental illness after he got married at the age of twenty. He had three previous attacks. The first attack was about twenty-three or four years old. One day, after drinking alcohol, he suddenly hit his head with a bowl, causing blood to flow. His face was like a martial arts fanatic. During the second and third attacks, he only cried or laughed, and each time he was forced to sleep for a while and then recovered. This action was really a recurrence of an old illness. On September 30, he had dinner with my younger brother's family and drank alcohol. After the meal, he took a knife and went home. When he arrived in the alley, my wife happened to be going out of the house. He intended to attack, but my wife grabbed his collar. I heard the alarm at home and rushed out with a door bolt and knocked his shin, and he fell to the ground. I took his knife and called the police to arrest him. Then, according to Dr. Huang of the Public Works Department, Hu Fuzhang was sent to the hospital by the HSBC Police Station on the night of October 9 and sent back to the police station by the hospital on the 16th. During this period, Hu Fuzhang was hospitalized and repeatedly examined by doctors and reported by nurses. His daily life, diet, conversation, and actions were no different from ordinary people, and there was no sign of mental disorder. Therefore, it was concluded that he had no mental illness. Judge Wu asked again, "Is the defendant not suffering from mental illness, or does he have this disease but it has not been detected during this period?" Dr. Huang replied that if he did have this disease, there must be unusual actions that could be observed during these few days, but he showed nothing. Judge Wu then asked again, "If there is mental illness that has not been detected, can it be detected by diagnosis within seven days?" The doctor replied, "It is difficult to be certain, but it would be more certain if the examination period were longer." Next, according to Sun Kui Fang, the report he prepared on the examination of the defendant was said to have been too lengthy. In fact, according to medical principles, the report was still too brief. Mental illness and neurological disease are two different types of diseases. Patients with mental illness are caused by stimulation of the brain, while neurological disease must have an action. Therefore, mental illness is not easy to diagnose and must refer to the events of his life. That is why the report detailed his infection with syphilis and smoking, etc. Syphilis is a very dishonorable disease. The patient's mental state is certainly extremely unpleasant, and the onset of this disease also has different durations. The brief one recovers in a moment and is most difficult to detect. Those whose onset is long-lasting and does not heal are easier to examine. Sun also listed the theory to cite evidence. After the interrogation, Judge Wu picked up his pen and said, "Whether Hu Fuzhang has mental illness and whether he took the knife home this time due to mental illness, a deadline of two months is set for the forensic doctor to conduct a detailed identification with the two doctors of the Public Works Department Hospital and issue an identification report as evidence for review."

Case of a Female Teacher Abandoned 116

Zhu Haisheng has three golden houses in Shanghai. There is another hair wife living in the Jiangwan countryside. Ni Xiuzhen, a female teacher at Binhai Elementary School in this city, has filed a lawsuit in the Special District Court against Zhu Haisheng for seduction and abandonment. According to Ni Xiuzhen's report, Zhu Haisheng, 32 years old, is a foreman at the Ruirong Iron Factory and earns a considerable monthly income. Therefore, his hair wife lives in the Jiangwan countryside, and he has three golden houses in Shanghai. The first is in Shende Lane, Huade Road, the second is Ni Xiuzhen, and the third is in Yulin Lane, Pingliang Road. Another child, one year and five months old, was born to Zhu and another person and is now taken back to Huade Road for foster care. As for Ni Xiuzhen, her hometown is Nanjing, her father died four years ago, and her family is poor. Since childhood, her younger brother studied at Wushi Elementary School, and then she supported the Xingnv School before dropping out and taking a teaching position at Wushi. This was three years ago. After that, she took a teaching position at Binhai Elementary School and met Zhu Haisheng. The feelings between the two became increasingly warm and they cohabited. However, because the wedding was not officially held, Ni feared her mother's opposition and concealed the matter, saying that she lived at the school. Last winter, she became pregnant and dropped out of school. Her mother still thought she was teaching at the school. This spring, Zhu gradually became estranged from her, pretending to be busy with factory affairs. Initially, she did not expect that Zhu had built a third golden house in Pingliang Road since cohabiting with Ni the year before. After various efforts, he had not revealed it. Since June of this year, Ni gave birth to a child at Guangren Hospital, and Zhu disappeared to Ni's place, and the monthly allowance was also cut off. Ni visited the factory many times, but Zhu refused to see her, claiming to be ill. At this point, Ni realized that he had two other golden houses in Shanghai, but it was too late to regret. After Ni filed a lawsuit with the court, Zhu tried to persuade her through others, willing to settle for 400 gold. However, Ni requested 5,000 yuan in alimony and waited for Zhu Haisheng to be summoned to court this Friday for further verification.

Apprentice Electrocuted to Death in Cellar 120

Corpse Found the Next Day

Chest Became Bluish-Purple

Lin Jiashan, a machine mechanic at Sassoon House, left his apprentice Ye Changrong in the machine room of the cellar at the address on the 8th of this month to find an iron bar. Ye took a flashlight with him because the cellar was quite dark. The electrical wire on the light leaked, causing Ye to be electrocuted. Because there was no one in the cellar at the time, no one knew until the next morning when a mechanic entered the cellar and saw Ye lying on the ground, his chest turning bluish-purple. Knowing that he had been electrocuted, he reported it to everyone and then to the Main Police Station. The detectives went to investigate and carried Ye's body to the autopsy office on Faelon Road. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Xu Mei of the Special District Court came to the office to inspect the body. After taking his seat, Lin Jiashan arrived at the case to testify and prove that the deceased was electrocuted in the cellar. According to Wang Lieming, the deceased's cousin, the deceased's brother was buying a coffin and could not come to the case, so I can take the lead. Also, Bei Quilai, the Western assistant mechanic of Sassoon, made several statements. Prosecutor Xu ordered the forensic doctor to examine the case again and again and determined that it was an electrocution. Then he announced that the deceased Ye Changrong had been identified by the forensic doctor as electrocuted, and the body was taken by the cousin Wang Lieming for coffin burial.

Jianghua Encountered Bandits and Escaped Danger 129

The China Merchants Bureau's Yangtze River steamer Jianghua, en route from Shanghai to Hankou, encountered bandits at approximately 10:00 AM yesterday when passing Jiujiang, near Huangzhou Cai Dian. As the ship was navigating upstream, the bandits planned to劫 (rob) the vessel. Initially, the bandits fired warning shots at the Jianghua, intending to force it to stop. However, the captain of the Jianghua, Wang Muzong, fearing the danger of being robbed, immediately ordered the driver to proceed upstream at full speed. The bandits on the shore then switched to firing cannons, launching eight consecutive shots at the ship. The situation was extremely perilous, and all passengers on board lay prone in their cabins, afraid to move. Fortunately, the driver accelerated to full speed, managing to evade the cannon fire. None of the eight shots hit the ship, a truly fortunate outcome. However, the crew members were deeply alarmed. Yesterday's telegram from Shanghai reported that the Jianghua had safely escaped danger and was heading towards Hankou.

Disputes over Water Rate Increases in the Concession 130

Ignoring public opinion, the water company has set a deadline for collecting the increased water fees. The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers' Association in the foreign concession received a letter yesterday from taxpayer Wu Jishun regarding the Shanghai Waterworks Company in the public concession setting a deadline to collect the increased water fees. The impact of this action could potentially lead to disputes. We have extracted and recorded the relevant correspondence below:

Wu Jishun's Letter to the Ratepayers' Association:

Regarding the unreasonable water price increase by the water company, your esteemed association has repeatedly engaged in negotiations. Now, the company has suddenly sent a notice to each household, stating, "If you do not comply with the increased payment by November 28th of this year, water supply will be suspended." As a taxpayer within the concession, Jishun believes that the increased water price should not be paid until your association reaches a resolution. We should adhere to the principles of your esteemed association and not deviate to undermine public opinion.

The Ratepayers' Association's Reply to Wu Jishun:

Having received your letter of November 9th, we wish to inform you that before the audit of water prices is completed and a decision is made to increase them, payments should continue at the original rate (i.e., 6% of the rent). Our association has already stated to the Shanghai Waterworks Company that the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce has rejected the increase, and the Shanghai Real Estate Association has repeatedly published announcements to that effect. The company's warning to users, setting a deadline with the threat of water suspension, is tantamount to strangling people to seize their property. How can anyone not feel resentment and rise up to fight for their rights? Please refuse to pay the increased water fees and do not succumb to threats, as we actively negotiate in accordance with principles of justice.

The Ratepayers' Association's Letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council:

Having received a letter from Mr. Wu Jishun stating that the Shanghai Waterworks Company has suddenly sent a notice to each household stating, "If you do not comply with the increased payment by November 28th of this year, water supply will be suspended," we wish to inform you that residents, both Chinese and foreign, have voiced their opposition to this water price increase. Therefore, an audit has been initiated to seek a peaceful resolution. At the beginning of the audit, our association stated to the Shanghai Waterworks Company that "before the audit is completed and a decision is made to increase prices, water prices should continue to be collected at the original rate (i.e., 6% of the rent). If it is later deemed necessary to increase prices, supplementary payments will be made." The company has disregarded this statement and has recently issued a concrete written warning to users, threatening water suspension. Water is an essential element of human life, almost as important as air. The company's threat of water suspension to force users to pay the increased water fees is like strangling people to seize their property. What desire cannot be fulfilled? However, the pursuit of life is a natural instinct. If the company insists on implementing its actions, which are tantamount to strangling people to seize the increased water fees, users, in order to safeguard their lives, will inevitably be forced to resist. What will become of public order? We hereby request that you investigate and seriously consider appropriate measures to mitigate this significant potential risk.

Overseas Chinese Federation 131

Requesting Assistance from the Newspaper Guild in the Xiao Case

Refusing to Publish Advertisements for Java Company and Ship Import/Export News

The Overseas Chinese Federation sent a letter to the local Newspaper Guild yesterday, stating: "Our country's female teacher, Ms. Xiao Xin'an, was brutally assaulted by the Dutch second mate of the Java Company's ship 'Tjibadak.' Your esteemed guild's newspapers have provided detailed coverage, with some publishing critical articles and others writing satirical pieces. The entire nation is deeply appreciative. Our federation and other organizations believe that verbal and written condemnation is sufficient to support the extension of justice, and boycotts and disconnections can serve as a backing after negotiations. We have repeatedly appealed, and we understand that the advertising department and the shipping schedule section are still publishing advertisements for the Java Company and the import/export news of its Java-class ships. It is not that they are unwilling to express sympathy, but because your esteemed guild has not yet convened a meeting to decide on the matter, there is still a waiting period. In order to achieve national unity, our federation has sent representative Lin Youren to your esteemed guild to discuss assistance. We were instructed by your esteemed guild to submit another letter, which we will certainly do. Therefore, we earnestly request that your esteemed guild, considering that the assault on Ms. Xiao is not only a personal disgrace to her but also a disgrace to the entire Chinese nation, approve the early convening of an emergency temporary meeting to accommodate our request. Starting immediately, unanimously refuse to publish advertisements for the Java Company and the import/export news of its ships 'Tjibadak,' 'Tjikareng,' 'Tjisandari,' 'Tjifcdas,' 'Tjipanas,' and 'Tjiliwong,' in order to vent public outrage. The faith of compatriots at home and abroad in your esteemed guild and its newspapers will continue to grow day by day. We would appreciate it if you could indicate whether this is feasible."

Tianyuan Electrochemical Plant Officially Opens Yesterday 132

Will Make Great Contributions to the Industrial Sector

Shanghai merchants Wu YunChu, Zhu Ziqian, Shen Yichang, Zhang Yiyun, Wang Dongyuan, etc., recognizing the severe shortage of industrial raw materials in our country, pooled their resources to establish the Tianyuan Electrochemical Plant on Baililan Road in Western Shanghai, specializing in the production of industrial products such as hydrochloric acid and caustic soda. The plant is large in scale, fully equipped, and has been under preparation for a year. The various products have been repeatedly tested by experts and are highly suitable for industrial use. Yesterday, the plant held its official opening ceremony at the Yipinxian restaurant, inviting guests from all walks of life. Among those present were Zheng Hongnian, Vice Minister of Industry and Commerce; Zhao Jinqing, representative of Minister Kong; Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau; Zhou Zijing, representative of the Central Research Institute; Guo Chengen, Director of the Arsenal; Yang Rumei; Shen Xiongqing; Wu Renzhi; Zhang Wuxin; Li Yunshu; Chang Jinqu; Zheng Shouzhi; Zou Bingwen; Cao Liangxia; and representatives from various paper-making, dyeing, and weaving factories, as well as British, American, and Japanese guests, totaling over two hundred people. The atmosphere was lively and bustling. After three rounds of wine, Zhu Ziqian, Chairman of the Board of Directors, Shen Yichang, Wang Dongyuan, and others delivered welcoming speeches, thanking the guests. At around 3:00 PM, the attendees dispersed and traveled to the plant in cars provided by the factory to observe the opening ceremony. They arrived at the plant at 3:30 PM and proceeded to the auditorium for a meeting. Director Wu of the plant respectfully read the will of Dr. Sun Yat-sen and reported on the establishment process. Zhao Jinqing, representing Minister Kong of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, then delivered a speech on behalf of the minister, stating that the electrical and chemical industry is closely related to the progress of civilization. For example, aluminum was once considered a rare and valuable metal, making it impractical for manufacturing tools. Since the invention of the electrolytic aluminum process by the American Hall in 1890, everyday utensils such as cookware have been completely replaced by aluminum, which users find convenient. The price of aluminum has plummeted. In 1855, it was valued at fifty pounds sterling per kilogram, but by the end of the nineteenth century, it had dropped to one shilling. Most surprisingly, as the price of aluminum fell, the profits of aluminum smelting companies increased, demonstrating that both production and consumption benefit from electrochemistry. In China, apart from electroplating, industries such as electrolysis and electrometallurgy are virtually non-existent. Mr. Wu YunChu has uniquely pioneered this factory, opening a new chapter in China's electrochemical industry. His spirit is truly admirable. I have always placed great emphasis on basic industries. During the Third Plenary Session, I drafted a plan for state-owned basic industries. At this industrial and commercial conference, there were many proposals to encourage privately owned basic industries, indicating that the Chinese people are gradually paying more attention to this matter. Caustic soda and hydrochloric acid, two products of the Tianyuan plant, are important raw materials in basic industries. The fact that the private sector can establish such a plant is commendable, and the government should do its utmost to encourage and protect it. After the speech, the attendees proceeded to the boiler room for the opening ceremony. Zhao Jinqing and Pan Gongzhan performed the fire-lighting ceremony, accompanied by the sound of firecrackers. After the ceremony, photographs were taken, and the event concluded.

Chairman Tong Xingbai opened the meeting with formal procedures. The chairman and representatives from various districts and branches reported on past work and future plans. After the reports, they discussed and resolved over thirty important cases, concluding the meeting after 6:00 PM.

Scheduled Memorial Service for Fan Zhengluo 134

Wang Yufen, Xu Qin, Shen Zengyi, Ren Liping, Zhang Mingqin, Tong Zikun, Yi Zuanren, Cao Runcang, Gao Yunlv, Zhu Yaoting, Chen Zikuan, Gang Yusong, Zhang Jiafu, Yao Benyuan, Fan Ningshu, Ye Weiyi, Ding Yaxian, Gu Zhenzhong, and others announce a memorial service for Comrade Fan Zhengluo:

The 12th of this month marks the most memorable anniversary of our comrade Fan Zhengluo's martyrdom. Time passes quickly, and a year has gone by. We, the comrades, mourn the passing of this man, deeply saddened by the approaching day. Several years ago, Mr. Fan, residing in Henan, was angered by the British exploitation and tirelessly campaigned, resulting in the miners' strike. At that time, his ambition could overwhelm powerful merchants, and his actions were sufficient to gain the trust of his peers. Had he been able to fulfill his potential and extend his influence, would the people of Henan alone have relied on him? Yet, he was assassinated by treacherous individuals, his great ambition concealed and unfulfilled, cut short in his prime. This is not only Mr. Fan's misfortune but also our shared grief. We undertake this action to lament the passing of those who cannot be revived and to hope that future generations will carry on. Mr. Fan has passed away, but we hope that those who will rise in his place will be our hope, and that is what we deeply desire. On this afternoon at 2:00 PM, a memorial service will be held at the Guandi Temple in Laoximen. If you have couplets, please send them in advance.

It is the only large-scale fine machinery factory in our country. The factory recently completed preparations and held its opening ceremony yesterday. Wanguo Company Releases Picture Cards 137

The Wanguo Trading Company at No. 9 Bei Wangyi Ma Lane, inside the Old North Gate in Shanghai, recently released a large batch of large and small colorful lithographic art picture cards, numbering in the hundreds, which are exquisitely beautiful. The large-size cards are divided into four types: fashionable women, scenery, gods and Buddhas, and portraits of great figures. Each type has ten sets of five cards each, priced at one yuan. The small-size cards are divided into three types: fashionable beauty, classical beauty, and nude beauty. Each type has two sets of eight cards each, also priced at one yuan. There are also dozens of various copper-edged and exquisitely framed screens depicting figures, history, couplets, landscapes, and flowers and birds. Each type has ten sets, with each set consisting of three panels, each panel with four paintings, totaling twelve paintings, also priced at one yuan. In addition, there are many types of popular education picture cards, covering historical news comprehensively, including "General Chiang Kai-shek's Northern Expedition" and "Portraits of Emperors and Empresses of the Shun Qing Dynasty," which are all treasures of the time. They are now divided into eight major sets, with each set consisting of fifty cards, also priced at one silver dollar. For mail orders from other cities, please specify the number of sets. Each set will incur an additional registration and postage fee of 14 cents.

News from Various Labor Unions 138

Five Labor Unions: Shanghai Shipping Timber Industry, Xiang Sheng Ironworks, Qiu Xin Shipyard, He Xing Shipyard, Rui Rong Ironworks, and other five labor unions issued a declaration regarding the Xin Dingchang case: (Omitted above) This case of the brutal killing of boatman Xin Dingchang by French sailors demonstrates the imperialists' contempt for our people's lives, treating them worse than dogs. Now that Dingchang has been brutally murdered, it is indeed a great misfortune that the weak are preyed upon by the strong. However, we and other unions, while still alive, should take the Xin case as a warning, grit our teeth, and vow to support the diplomacy behind the scenes. In the shortest possible time, we demand that the French government provide generous compensation to Dingchang's family for funeral expenses, and, in accordance with the precedents of our country compensating foreigners, provide alimony to his family. Furthermore, the perpetrators should be severely punished and a formal apology issued to our country. In addition, they must be responsible for guaranteeing that no similar incidents occur in the future. If there is no satisfactory resolution, we vow to fight the French imperialists to the death. We hope that all compatriots across the country will rise up together and pursue this matter to the end. This is our declaration.

Silk Factory: The Workers' Union in the Pudong district held a meeting of representatives from various factories yesterday, chaired by Chen Zongxiang and others. Chen Xiupu, Chen Zongxiang, Qian Xutian, Li Bingyao, Wu Yansun, Zhu Xizhang, and Chen Yanzhang were elected as committee members; (3) The employer's violation of the established regulations, deducting benefits, and suspending meals, etc., violate government factory regulations. Resolution: The special committee should promptly negotiate the matter; (4) The labor union's finances have been reported separately by the former accounting department. There is very little remaining. The autumn regular fees should be paid to facilitate operations. Resolution: Each branch will collect and submit the fees within three days by their respective responsible persons; (5) Corrupt elements are undermining the labor movement. In this tense work situation, measures should be formulated as soon as possible to facilitate operations. Resolution: Ten representatives were elected on the spot to investigate and deal with the matter in each branch.
