Free Talk

Laughing it Off 141

— Hai Ke

Husband (searching all around the desk): Hey, that's strange. I just took out a four-cent stamp to put on this letter. How did it disappear in the blink of an eye?

Wife: Open your mouth and look in the mirror. It's stuck to your tongue.

Girl A: My fiancé is nearsighted, very nearsighted. He can't see anything clearly unless he puts it right up to his eyes.

Girl B: Ah, that explains it. That's why he got engaged to you.

Wife: Look how hard our child is working today! He's been writing since this morning, and he's been at it for two hours straight without stopping.

Husband: Yes, that's all my doing. Otherwise, would he be working so hard?

Wife: How did you get him to do that?

Husband: I told him the New Year is coming soon, and he needs to make a list of everything he wants for me. So he can't stop writing.

Doctor: Scarlet fever is an extremely dangerous disease, especially after recovery. You have to be extra careful and constantly worried.

Patient: Exactly. These past few days, I've been worried about you handing over that medical bill.

A Visit to the Tianyi Pavilion Library in Ningbo 142

— Bao Sixin

Among the oldest private libraries in China, the Tianyi Pavilion of the Fan family in Ningbo is the most enduring. The pavilion was founded during the Jiajing reign of the Ming Dynasty by Fan Qin, who was titled "Dai Lang." Qin, whose given name was Yaoqing and courtesy name was Dongming, was a Jinshi graduate in the eleventh year of Jiajing. He successively held prominent positions such as Right Vice Minister of the Ministry of War. He once opposed Guo Xun and was known for his strong will. Even Yan Song was deeply afraid of him. Qin loved collecting books and built the Tianyi Pavilion to purchase rare editions from across the country, classified into the four categories of classics, history, philosophy, and literature. He was particularly adept at collecting commentaries on the classics and collections of poems and essays by early scholars that had not been passed down. However, the books in the pavilion consisted mostly of old items from the Wanjuange library of the Feng family in Chengxi. The Feng family was descended from the Qingmin Duke and produced prominent figures in each generation, so their collection of books was incomparably rich. It is a pity that their descendant, Daosheng, suffered from a mental illness late in life and became so obsessed with books and ink that he lost his family's wealth. Nearly 60% of the books in the Wanjuange library, including Song dynasty transcriptions, were stolen by his students. Later, a major fire destroyed much of what remained. Sir Fan had previously copied books from Daosheng, so he used what remained to add to his own pavilion. He also copied books from Mr. Huang Lizhou to supplement his collection. Although he was unable to restore the Feng family's library to its former glory, he was still a dominant figure in Eastern Zhejiang. During the late Qing Dynasty, his descendant, the Minister of the Board of Civil Office, Duke Lu, continued to add to the collection. During the Qianlong reign, the Siku Quanshu (Complete Library of the Four Treasuries) was compiled, and the books in the pavilion were copied and added to the imperial library. Duke Lu was awarded the Jishu Jicheng (Collected Writings of the Jishu Studio) by the emperor. During the Taiping Rebellion, the pavilion was damaged and the books were scattered. Although many were redeemed through various means, it was impossible to prevent them from being lost. During the Guangxu reign, Xue Fucheng, an observer from Wuxi, took advantage of his spare time in Eastern Zhejiang to visit the pavilion and lament the loss of the books, realizing how difficult it would be to purchase more. He then established categories and assigned Qian Nianqu from Gui'an to proofread the books. It took two years and three revisions to complete the existing catalogue of the Tianyi Pavilion. Since the founding of the Republic of China, the pavilion has been burgled twice, and 60% of the books have been lost, with the most prized volumes stolen. Yang Ziyi, the mayor of Ningbo, has proposed reorganizing the catalogue for publication. On October 21st, Bao Sixin, who happened to be in Ningbo, was able to visit the pavilion and felt fortunate to have the opportunity to browse the collection. The pavilion is located west of Moon Lake, with beautiful scenery of ponds and rocks in front. A plaque reading "Treasure Book Building" hangs below the pavilion, with a couplet inscribed with imperial approval: "A grand sight of a city of books, rarely seen in the human world." There are also two couplets by the historian Quan Zuwang: "Looking south, the dense forests are turned into stone paths, and the treasures are all returned to the outstanding pavilion. Looking west, the city of Qi should lament that one's floating life has fallen far behind the high gate," and "A hundred thousand volumes of silk-covered books are arranged in order, laughing at the unworthiness of green bamboo and dark clouds. For three hundred years, the pure and secret light has brightly connected the eastern building, and the green lotus pond is not far away." The upper floor of the pavilion is where the books are stored. Normally, the pavilion is only opened once a year to air the books, and outsiders are not allowed to enter. This time, thanks to the special permission of the owner, the pavilion was temporarily opened. Mr. Fan Luqi, the head of the sixth branch of the Fan family, led the visitors to the upper floor. The pavilion consists of six rooms connected as one, separated by bookshelves. Cloud stones are placed under the shelves to prevent moisture. The pavilion is divided into six rooms, taking the meaning of "Heaven is born from water, and Earth is formed by six." The name "Tianyi" is also derived from this. After entering the pavilion, the owner first presented the "Victory Picture of Pacifying the Hui Region," which was awarded by the emperor. The picture is meticulously painted and contains an imperial inscription. It is a rare sight. I had previously seen a similar picture at the Xujiahui Library in Shanghai. Next, I read portraits of ancient emperors, famous officials, and Confucian scholars. The inscriptions seemed to be drawn with a hook, so I guessed they were imitations. Then, I opened the shelves and read the books. There were mostly Ming dynasty editions, with very few Song dynasty editions, and many were incomplete. Secret books and manuscripts, such as Cai Guangzhi's "Treatise," were not available elsewhere and were truly precious. Due to the limited time, I was unable to examine them in detail. Finally, I viewed the steles, with the Tang dynasty Shenlong edition of Chu Suiliang's copy of the Preface to the Orchid Pavilion Poems being the most valuable. There were also wooden plaques from the Fan family's collection, but unfortunately, many were decayed. After the visit, I bid farewell to the owner and returned. Mr. Huang Lizhou and the historian Quan Zuwang both praised the Tianyi Pavilion in their records, and its reputation was highly regarded by scholars. It is a pity that after several disasters and thefts, the precious books were scattered and difficult to restore to their former glory. Now, Mayor Yang is considering reorganizing the catalogue to further organize the collection. This is something that those concerned about the country are pleased to hear. Therefore, I wrote this record to commemorate this great event.

Record of the Xu-Huang Wedding 143

— Lu Jingqing

The sixth of this month was the day for the wedding of Mr. Huang Cuojiu's daughter. The Qian and Kun halls of Yipinxian Restaurant were reserved. The groom, Mr. Xu, courtesy name Xiaochu, had experience in literature, politics, and business. He is currently employed at the Sino-French Pharmacy. Mr. Pei Lishen, the groom's father, is a famous lawyer from Suzhou and has served as the Director of the Land Bureau of Anhui Province. The bride, Ms. Gengbao, is a high-achieving graduate of the Sino-Western Girls' School. This match is a perfect couple, a pearl and jade alliance. Although there were light rain and wind during the day, the guests were already crowded. Prominent figures from political and business circles in Beijing and Shanghai all personally came to offer their congratulations. The music provided by the Moteli Company played in turns in the hall, melodious and pleasant. From morning onwards, each table was set with Western pastries made by the Maikesikai Candy Company, surpassing those made by Sullivan. The guests ate their fill of the delicious food, and by the time of the luncheon, almost everyone was unable to eat any more.

In the two halls, both old and new, there were countless banners, plaques, and screens on the walls. The large banners donated by Zhang Jingjiang, Chu Minyi, Sun Binqi, and Xu Shiying were particularly eye-catching to the guests. Yu Youren's couplet, "Weaving dew into pearls, spreading the sunset into curtains, picking duckweed to fill baskets, brewing wine to fill goblets," and Wang Yiting's couplet, "Jujubes and sesame seeds can feed guests, rare flowers and trees guard the eternal spring," and Lin Kanghou's couplet, "Three thousand pairs of bejeweled shoes fill the auspicious family, and brightly colored carriages fill the gate," were all beautiful works. My humble work was a painting of mandarin ducks, titled "Jade Maiden Smiles at Mandarin Ducks, Urging the Heart to Release Fragrant Petals, Warm Curtains and Hibiscus Quilt, Emerald Pair Sharing Dreams Through the Long Night." On this day, guests came from morning to night without end. There were thousands of staff members from the Great World, the Day and Night Bank, various Chinese and Western pharmacies, Jiufu Company, Jiuzhitang Zhai, and the Tainwu Stage. When the ceremony was held, they lined up in an orderly manner, resembling fish swimming in a row.

When the clock struck five, the wedding officiant, Mr. Shao Lizi, arrived on time. I have known him for many years, and we happily reminisced. The time passed quickly. Then, I heard loud music, indicating that the wedding car had arrived. At the wedding ceremony, the sound of musical instruments rang out as the wedding march was played. The matchmakers, Ma Bingxun and Zhou Mengbai, walked in front, followed by the groom and bride, and the attendants in order. Xie Jixiang, the groom's attendant, with his handsome demeanor, was the focus of the crowd's attention. Leng Yuren gave a wonderful speech as a guest speaker, with witty remarks that were met with thunderous applause. Mr. Shao Lizi gave a long speech, encouraging the newlyweds to love each other. His words were heartfelt and could be described as the ultimate praise.

In the evening, there were various performances at the Great World, which were very exciting. After the banquet was over, I, along with Mr. Leng and Mr. Gaoye Zhang, went to Mr. Xu's residence on Yuyuan Road for the bridal chamber teasing. The guests indulged in playful banter, and the room was filled with suggestive remarks. The blushing bride and groom were forced to kiss each other, but the attempt ultimately failed.

Records of Odd People and Strange Habits 144

— Shen Zhenhu

People have different hobbies and different loves. However, there is no one who likes to eat poisonous things like snakes and insects. If there is, then it is the odd person Hailancha who is currently performing in public at the Great World. He has come to Shanghai from the sea, and the whole city is buzzing with excitement. Yesterday, the owner of the Great World asked Mr. Li Yaoliang to invite the press to watch. The guests were warmly welcomed. First, they were served cakes specially made by the Maikesikai Company, which tasted especially good. It was a great pleasure to both eat and watch. Therefore, I wrote this record.

The Origin of the Odd Person: The teahouse was crowded, and for a moment, it became lively. First, a certain gentleman described Hailan's brief history, saying that there was a Hailancha in the early Qing Dynasty who liked to eat living creatures. The current Hailancha is probably his descendant. He escaped into the mountains as a child and lived off insects, animals, fruits, and raw blood. He was discovered by people in the mountains at the age of twenty-two and has been living among them for five years. He has learned a little human language. When asked, he says that he is a Manchurian from Qingdao. His voice is loud and clear. However, looking at his clothes, he is the same as ordinary people and has completely shed the wildness of a person from the mountains.

The Horrific Performance: After a certain gentleman finished speaking, he took out two crawling insects from underground and handed them to Hailan. Hailan, wearing a long gown, velvet hat, and sunglasses, held the insects and threw them into his mouth. He chewed them as if they tasted quite good. In a short time, he swallowed them completely. He then swallowed two tree root insects and ate them as before. Then, a cage of mice was brought out, squeaking. Hailan took one of them and put it in his mouth. With a bang, the mouse's head was broken off, and blood dripped down. The mouse was still rolling on the ground. Hailan chewed and swallowed the head, bones, and fur. Then, a dove was brought out, which he ate as if it were a mouse. His teeth were like sharp blades. The most horrific thing to witness was killing a rabbit. Hailan took a large white rabbit and grabbed its four feet with both hands. The rabbit cried out. Hailan bit the rabbit's neck and tore out a mouthful of fur, revealing red flesh. Then, he slowly ate the meat from its back with relish, while the rabbit was still wriggling. He then ate two poisonous snakes. The crowd applauded and dispersed. Hailan can be called an odd person with strange habits.

Record of Impressions of West Lake (5) 145

— Huijian

At eight o'clock on the eighth day, I went to the Zhejiang Highway Bureau at the New Market to purchase tickets for the Haining Tide Watching bus, each ticket costing three dollars and twenty cents. The bus was smaller than the usual public bus, only accommodating seventeen passengers. At eight fifteen, the bus departed, passing through the city of Hangzhou and exiting Qingtai Gate. Haining is about ninety miles from Hangzhou, and the journey takes two hours. The highway is newly built and not too bumpy. After leaving Qingtai Gate, both sides of the road are lined with bamboo forests, which only end at Qibao. The sunlight penetrates the bamboo, making the bus window as dark as night. At ten o'clock, we arrived at Dadongmen in Haining. Many tourists had already arrived. The Haining County Government had set up a reception area beside the central tea garden, on the levee, which was very crowded. The tide-watching platform was divided into three sections: one built by the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureau, one by the Zhejiang Highway Bureau, and one as a general viewing platform, each accommodating hundreds of people. Several viewing pavilions were set up on the eastern embankment, like private boxes, with large white paper signs reading "Haining Local Court Reception Area." I stood there for a while, admiring the view of the Qiantang River, a thousand miles of white, a truly magnificent scene. Opposite us was the territory of Xiaoshan, with a pointed mountain between Haining and Xiaoshan, which could be clearly distinguished with a telescope. Old Lan, feeling hungry, went from behind the Zhenhai Pagoda to Chunxi Gate Street for a snack. Seeing that it was still early, he entered the city and visited the God of the Sea Temple, where someone had set up a domestic goods market, which was simple and unremarkable. Behind the temple was a circus that charged admission, with a notice stating "National Arts Division." We were all amused. Returning to the central tea garden, we passed a residence where an art exhibition was being held, with tickets costing six and a half silver dollars. Xia Shi showed a badge, and the ticket price was halved, claiming it was preferential treatment. The exhibition only contained a few dozen ordinary paintings and calligraphy, and even Sun Baoqi's calligraphy of a longevity poem was considered a work of art. Tourists bought tickets to pass the time, so it was perhaps a speculative technique. Around eleven o'clock, we returned to the levee, and the crowd grew even larger. There was a couplet at the levee gate: "Breaking ten thousand miles of waves, an empty alley of ten thousand people; coming in a single line of tide, defending a belt of dikes." The meaning was new, but the wording was slightly awkward. Beside it was the "Three Visits Pavilion," built by Haining officials in the past to flatter Qu Yingguang, because Qu had visited this place three times to inspect the dike project when he was the Governor of Zhejiang Province. I went up to the Highway Bureau viewing platform and sat down with Xia, engaging in discussions of the past and present. At twenty minutes past twelve, we suddenly saw a silver ribbon on the east side of the river, as still as if it was frozen, and the crowd shouted, "The tide is coming!" Ten minutes later, the silver ribbon gradually thickened, and we could hear the roar of the tide, rolling in from several miles away. Since it was inconvenient to take pictures on the platform, I quickly jumped to the side of the levee to set up my camera. The tide was not very high that day, but its momentum was fierce, sharp and powerful, enough to make people feel uneasy. After the first wave passed, a second wave followed. The second wave was not as neat as the first, but its surging momentum was even greater. The crowd watched until the tide receded far away, and then everyone returned home with a feeling of completion. I quickly got on the bus, and we returned to Hangzhou around one o'clock. The return journey was blocked by traffic, and the dust filled the air, choking our noses. After arriving in Hangzhou, everyone looked disheveled. I rushed to a bathhouse for a bath. Xia and Old Lan needed to go to the city to buy umbrellas, fans, silk, and cotton items to give as gifts, so I went to the lakeside park alone and took a boat to Gushan Island again. It was three thirty in the afternoon, and the lake was as quiet as a long summer day.

Warmth in the Heart (312) 146

— Bao Tianxiao

Episode Fifteen: Tears Fall in All Directions, Red Feelings of Sorrow; Hearts are Captivated, Lingering Green Intentions

Yuebinlou could be considered a Northern-style establishment, with all the managers and employees being northerners. Their service to customers was known to be attentive. Whenever a customer stepped into their restaurant, several people wearing blue cloth robes, like greeters, would stand respectfully, welcoming them whether they were familiar or not, saying, "You're here!" or "Long time no see!" When you finished eating and were leaving, they would also stand respectfully, sending you off with a courteous demeanor, saying, "Goodbye!" or adding, "Please come and visit us often!" All the waiters were mostly from Tianjin or Shandong. When you gave them instructions, they would always answer with a "Zhe! Zhe! Zhe!" Some say northerners are good at being subservient, but that's not entirely true. However, restaurants rely on attentive service, so people will naturally come. If you have a rigid and unyielding demeanor, who would want to see your face? Those waiters often made a high-pitched and drawn-out sound that made people laugh, and they also put on a comical expression so that customers couldn't get angry but would laugh it off. These were their special skills. Long Ziyun and his group often ate at Yuebinlou, so they were already familiar with the staff. When they entered, the manager downstairs would shout, "Fourth Master Long is here! Are there any seats upstairs?" The waiter downstairs would quickly reply, "Yes, there is!" displaying the air of a superior calling and inferiors responding from all directions. When they went upstairs, the staff would also consider the number of guests. If there were seven or eight people, they would lead them to a large room. If it was just three or four people having a drink, they would lead them to a small room, leaving the large room for larger groups. Some diners were familiar with the waiters, as if they were their regular customers. They would naturally come to greet Long Ziyun. When he entered, he told them that there were six or seven guests, so they led them to a large room along the balcony, busily changing to a round table and covering it with a bleached tablecloth, serving tea, melon seeds, and hawthorn fruit. They called that type of hawthorn fruit "red fruit," candied with honey. So they were busy serving the guests for a while before arranging the cups and chopsticks and asking the guests to order. Northern-style restaurants had several signature dishes, such as stir-fried fish slices with wine sauce, stir-fried shrimp, diced chicken with bean curd skin, etc. When hosting guests in Beijing or eating at a restaurant, each person would often order a dish. In addition to the basic dishes, the host would let each guest order a dish. People in Shanghai did not follow this custom. When they couldn't think of what to order, they would often ask the waiter to recommend some good dishes. Then the waiter would recite a string of dishes like a schoolchild reciting a text. Because they recited so quickly, it was difficult to consider the options, so you would ask them to recite it again, often several times. They didn't seem to mind.

The arrival of Hunan lotus seeds has been scarce recently. According to yesterday's telegraph, the price suddenly rose due to limited stock in Hankou. Nine Creek lotus seeds rose 23 taels per shi, and Changde lotus seeds rose 22 taels. Including all external fees, the price was almost twice as high as the Shanghai price. Because the market in this area is sluggish, the market remains flat. Yesterday's market price for Xiangze lotus seeds was 43-44 taels, Xiaozhou lotus seeds were 40 taels, Hengzhou lotus seeds were 39 taels, Nine Creek lotus seeds were 38 taels and a half, and Changde lotus seeds were 36 taels and a half. If sales improve in the future, the price will likely rise accordingly.

Silk and Tea: Shanghai Factories' Cables to Europe Have Not Yet Improved Situation 162

Yesterday, the foreign silk market in Shanghai was quiet. Due to the financial turmoil in Lyon, silk cables to Europe did not improve the Shanghai situation. European merchants adopted a wait-and-see approach. American merchants only purchased 30 bales of Sichuan yellow silk from the Jingchuan factory and 20 bales of Shanghai white silk from Huatong, etc. Due to high costs, merchants were unwilling to sell at a loss. Market sentiment was sluggish.

Milan Italian Silk Sales Sluggish 163

Daily silk prices are low, European merchants sell at low prices... Current silk prices continue to fall by 3-4 lire. Although sales of Italian silk in the Milan market to Europe have slightly improved, prices are still trending downwards. Although Central European and American exporters actively purchased existing silk last week, the price of Italian silk continues to fall by 3-4 lire due to lower Japanese silk prices. The price of Extra Grade silk is 500 lire per kilogram, Special Grade is 451 lire, and Superior Grade is 402 lire.

Total and Remaining Stock of Tea from Lu Zhuang Tea Houses 164

Tea from the Lu Zhuang tea houses is produced in the various regions of Yuanyuan, Tunxi, Yinxian, and Suian. It occupies a large portion of the foreign tea industry. Last year's production amounted to over 320,000 boxes. Due to the mid-term termination of the Russian merchant trade, the market fell sharply. However, the existing stock was not excessive even when new tea came on the market. The tea supply from the Lu source has now been cut off. The total amount of tea delivered to the tea houses is estimated to be 255,341 boxes, a decrease of 75,000 boxes compared to last year. 150,668 boxes have already been sold as of the above date. The remaining stock in the warehouses is 104,673 boxes. The Russian merchant trade has significant sales, and Morocco has not shipped many goods, so the remaining tea should be easy to sell. The amount and stock of each tea house are listed below: Warehouse Name: Amount Delivered, Amount Sold, Amount of Existing Stock. Hong Youyong: 46,541, 12,249, 34,292. Yong Shengchang: 21,632, 3,855, 17,777. Gong Sheng Yong: 36,722, 26,053, 10,669. Jia Yuan: 30,981, 14,866, 16,225. Yuan Fengrun: 20,821, 7,952, 12,866. Sheng Changsheng: 24,088, 13,625, 10,463. Fine Serge Fabric is Selling the Best 165

The cotton market at this factory has been stable in recent days. However, Tianzi Xiang cloth from Hubei has rebounded because of a scarce supply. This street has a daily demand of 30 packages, so supply cannot meet demand. Yesterday, it sold for 8 taels and 6 mace. 13-pound English cloth from Xiamen merchants was traded at 50 pieces at 6 taels and 1 mace. Coarse cloth was slightly soft compared to before, with three-yarn cloth opening at 4 taels and 7 mace, and Three Rabbit/Three Deer cloth at 4 taels and 7 mace and a half. Cotton cloth and fine twill fabric have been selling very little. However, Guang Bang merchants have been adding to the supply of Shu Bian Yu fine twill, which opened at 6 taels, 7 mace, and 7.5 fen. The existing stock of famous brand cloth is consistently lacking.

The market for East-West piece goods has become active again, with merchants searching for goods. Fine serge fabric is selling particularly well. Huxin Ting and Huanle are both at 3 mace and 1 fen, and Sanyou Tu is at 2 mace and 7 li and a half. 200 plus pieces have been traded between merchants from Changsha, Hankou and this street. Cotton thread has also become slightly firmer, with Fuhua Princess Color opening at 1 mace and 8 fen, Scarlet at 1 mace and 9 fen, Bird Beauty at 1 mace and 8 fen and 7 li and a half. Since the weather turned cold, the sales of bleaching powder from the door merchants have been very active. Double Child Deer requires 7 taels and 8 mace and a half, Watching Butterfly 7 taels and 8 mace, and Qilin 8 taels. Jiao Ye Ti Shu fell to 2 mace and 6 fen and a half, Magpie Bridge Meeting 2 mace and 7 fen and 2 li and a half. The Western goods board advanced another 20-30 pieces this street, priced at 2 mace and 2 fen and a half to 3 fen.

Rong Tai Top Grade Tribute Reaches 7 Taels 166

Yuan Qing top-grade tribute woolen fabric has been selling well in recent days. This is because merchants from this street have been purchasing it. The association's single and double sided sale prices are firm, because there is a shortage of stock in Shanghai, leading to a possible price increase. Shanghai Market

Market News 185

The Fashion Department of the Dasing Silk and Satin Bureau on Shili Road is known for its exquisitely crafted silk and satin fashions. The elegant ladies of Shanghai who wear them to perform dances at the Dahua Hotel and other high-class ballrooms are deeply praised by the general public. As autumn ends and winter approaches, the bureau has specially purchased the finest fur goods, and all kinds of fur materials suitable for making winter fashions are readily available. Recently, many ladies from all walks of life have been enthusiastically pre-ordering from the bureau. Those who want to make winter fashions will be very happy to hear this.

The Heli Food Company at the intersection of French Avenue and West Xinjiao Street declares that it has been in business for many years, specializing in various Chaozhou foods. Its bean paste buns and peanut candies are well-known in the market. Whenever peanuts are in season, it also offers a Chaozhou lard peanut candy, which is popular among people in Shanghai.

The Maoli Clothing Company below the Daya Building on Fourth Avenue declares that it specializes in making capes and overcoats. It employs famous artists to tailor new winter outfits and provides gorgeous evening dresses for rent. Many elegant ladies of Shanghai come to order them because the prices are very affordable.

The Western Food Department of the Chinese YMCA declares that, for the convenience of customers in the business and academic communities, it will add a Quik Lunch (i.e., American-style meals) to its lunch menu starting from the 15th of this month. The price is 65 cents per guest. It strives to select precious ingredients and cook in a hygienic manner. All members of the business and academic communities are welcome to patronize. The hours are from 10:00 AM to 2:00 PM daily, and the usual services will continue at other times.

The Maoli Women's Fashion Company below the Taiya Building on Fourth Avenue declares that it specializes in making new-style capes and overcoats. It employs fine art experts to tailor new clothes at low prices. Many Shanghai ladies come to order them, and the company's staff is very friendly.

The Dujinsheng Silk Weaving Factory declares that the Chrysanthemum Exhibition of Calligraphy and Painting, initiated by famous people in Shanghai, will be held on the second floor of the Nanjing Road National Products Department Store from the 8th to the 16th of this month. This is an unprecedented grand event. Dujinsheng, in view of the splendor of its exquisite and high-quality silk gift items displayed at the event, such as silk woven landscapes, figures, and colorful brocades, numbering no less than several hundred, has been receiving a constant stream of visitors since the opening and has been highly praised by people from all walks of life. The number of people placing orders with our factory in recent days has been very enthusiastic.

The Xinya Cantonese Restaurant at the intersection of North Sichuan Road and Qiujiang Road declares that it is good at preparing dishes and snacks, pays attention to hygiene, and cooks skillfully. It has long been praised and is well-known. Now, the owner of the restaurant has specially prepared stuffed crab shells to serve the public. The method involves taking the crab meat, adding ingredients, placing it in the crab shell, and then grilling it again. The method of eating is very simple without losing the original flavor of the crab, and it is not as greasy as crab roe.

Theater News 186

The World Grand Theater at the corner of Qingyun Road in Zhabei declares that, starting today, it will screen the first production of the Minghua Company, "Two Heroes of the Orient," also known as "The Great Thief Iron Arhat." It describes the heroes in the green woods who eliminate villains and help the weak in every detail. Not only is the plot tortuous, but the performance is also extremely realistic. The mechanisms in the film are unique, captivating viewers. At the same time, it will also show the latest and most satisfying work of the comical protagonist Lu Bielin from "The Scandalous History of the Revolving Palace," "The Great Disturbance in Morocco," which will make people laugh.

The Dadong Golden Lion Film Company declares that this year's great production, "The Legend of the Righteous Hero," is a martial arts and suspenseful love movie. The film features extremely magnificent and spectacular scenes and is truly a successful work in the film and drama industry. It is directed by Wang Fuqing and written by Yang Xiaozhong. Both Wang and Yang have long enjoyed a great reputation in the film industry. This joint effort will be a unique highlight for the silent domestic films. The entire cast of actors is extremely talented, and all performances are satisfactory and flawless. The film is scheduled to premiere today at the Central Grand Theater on Sixth Avenue. Those who love to watch good films should not miss this masterpiece.

Publishing News 187

Mr. Jin Kuansheng, director of the Shanghai Caoye Society at 34 Felun Road, held a wedding ceremony with Ms. Jiang Lijuan at the Catholic Church on Nanxun Road in Hongkou at 10:00 AM yesterday. In addition to going to congratulate him, the colleagues of the Caoye Society specially published a wedding commemorative issue. The content is exquisite and comes from the works of famous writers and fellow members, including Tang Zengshu's [Congratulatory Praise], Chuan Yanchang's [A Brief Account of Jin Kuansheng's Pre-Marriage], Zhu Yingpeng's congratulatory character [Textual Marriage], Zhang Ruogu's [Blessing a Happy Couple], Ms. Jin Guangjuan's [May You Both], Gao Zhenxiu's congratulatory poem, Shao Guanhua's [Eros and Light], Gu Shangxian's [The Pre-Marriage Him], Wang Tiehua's [My Dedication], Guo Lan's [Congratulations in a Small Utensil], Zheng Zhi's [Pouring a Glass of Wine] and [Strong Wine and Light Taste], Huang Huanruo's [Hua Wine Brews a Spring Scene], Mi Luo's [Protecting with the Two Words of Life as a Gift], and Tang Zengshu's [In Addition to Congratulations]. All newspaper vendors in this city are selling on consignment with an additional two cents for postage. The fourteenth issue of Caoye in three volumes has been published on the 8th.

Near the original site of the Municipal Government on Nanjing Road, Mr. Yu Shun'en and others organized a Chrysanthemum Association, displaying thousands of famous chrysanthemums and thousands of ancient and modern calligraphy and paintings. There are also elegant performances and dances by famous ladies to add to the fun. It has already opened yesterday, and the participants are quite enthusiastic. A special publication has been printed, edited by Cao Chigong and Zhang Yizai from the Literary Supply Society. The content includes photographic works of famous chrysanthemums and works by famous artists such as Ms. Yu Danhan. There are also various news about the association. The printing is exquisite and is sold at the venue, and also at the bookstore department of the National Products Department Store.

The Chongqing Bookstore on East Baoxing Road declares that the Natural Science and Social Science books it previously published were theoretically clear and have been praised by social figures. Now, it has published the first volume of "The History of World Culture," a new masterpiece by the famous American educator, Thorndike. Many universities in Europe and America have adopted it as a textbook. This book is as famous as Wells' "Outline of History," and the amount of material is roughly the same, but the price is very low. It is expected that the sales market will definitely be prosperous.

Social News

Why Edison Said Education in the Future Can Use Movies Instead of Books (Continued) 188

— Dr. Wei Zhong's Lecture, Notes by Yang Chuoran and Zhu Keliang

We are all like constables, doing whatever our managers tell us. We only know how to obey orders. Why? Because our brains are not good enough. Human brains are very inadequate. Revolutions throughout human history are all empty talk. Revolutions in history are not revolutions. It's just that there used to be an emperor, and then a few more emperors came along. The people of the Republic of China in history are all constables, revolting according to the orders of others. During the revolutionary period, they are still constables, still obeying orders. All the Republics of China, no matter which one in the world, are like this in revolutionary history. Why is this? Because human brains are too limited. Why are brains so inadequate? It is because, after thousands of years, there has been religion. How does religion diminish human brainpower? Religion severs the relationship between the natural world and the human body and brain. By cutting off this relationship, human brainpower is eliminated. This explanation is a scientific explanation because the human brain relies on the body, and the body relies on the natural world. Without the natural world, there is no human body; without the body, there is no brain. Constant use of the brain that has no relationship with the body and the natural world is sure to exhaust brainpower. Just look at bookworms: the deeper their learning, the more empty their speech. They utter many empty words, thinking that others cannot see the emptiness of their words. They only talk, not about facts. They cannot talk about facts; they do not understand any facts because their brains have been exhausted.

Now comes a very important part of the lecture.

Human brainpower has reached a point of complete inadequacy. If we know this, we can explain how [scholars] use any means to pretend to be intelligent. Those who are completely devoid of brainpower go everywhere searching for masks, using any means to prevent others from knowing they lack experience. They have never seen an animal but want to study zoology. The less they see animals, the more they want to study zoology. After studying, they know all the terms of zoology, and then others cannot detect that they have never actually seen an animal. There is nothing, but there are terms. Terms are like actors on stage wearing masks and pretending to be something. The inside of the mask is not necessarily what it seems, but from the outside, it looks very similar. Mr. Hu Shih once said that we should overthrow "name-based education." This can also partially prove that terms are the most dangerous masks for humans. For example, the more thoughtless I am, the more I use terms to conceal my lack of thought because terms come from books. The more thoughtless I am, the more I read books. If I didn't read books, others would be able to see that I have no thoughts, so I think it is important to read books. After reading European books, I know about Europe because the books prevent others from finding out that I actually know nothing about Europe. Plagiarizing the thoughts of others and gleaning the experiences of others to substitute for one's own thoughts and experiences is what reading is for. It means taking the thoughts of others to replace one's own thoughts and the experiences of others to replace one's own experiences; that is the purpose of reading books.

Therefore, people generally admire [books] very deeply. Thinking can be dispensed with, experience can be dispensed with; why not just use a little money to buy the thoughts and experiences of others? Wouldn't that be much more convenient? Using one's own thoughts to find one's own experiences requires so much effort. The body doesn't want to move, and the brain doesn't want to think. It's much better to buy books and read them, practice speaking, and the less you know about things, the better you can speak. Isn't that great? Isn't that much more convenient? Go investigate minerals? Too much trouble, you have to travel and be exposed to the sun, it's extremely annoying! It's better to buy a six-cent mineralogy book and read it at home. Much, much more convenient.

According to what was just said, since religion causes people's brainpower to be eliminated, they still need to do a second thing [to prevent others from knowing that they have no brainpower]: use books to make them seem like they have substituted their thoughts and experiences. Thus, under religious culture, most people never generate a single thought in their lives. They always have books to replace their own thoughts, so they are completely unaware that they have no thoughts. We can use an analogy to illustrate the greatest difficulty. For example, if I am sick and I know I am sick, I can be cured. But to be sick and not know it, thinking you are healthy—there is nothing more dangerous than that! Therefore, current young students just muddle through, going to class and reading books. Today they are students, tomorrow they are teachers. I ask them: [What is your brainpower like? What do you think about?] The person being asked will instead ask you: [Brainpower? What is brainpower?] They have no idea about brainpower at all because they have never used their brainpower while reading books. They have never used their own thoughts, they have only used the thoughts of others. They have only read books, they have never used their own thoughts, they have only used the brains of others. Now, education that requires people to read books is a way to eliminate human brainpower. This is very dangerous. Selling women to brothels is very wrong, but forcing men into libraries is even worse. For example, a prostitute's body is very ruined, but she puts on very good clothes, using external gorgeous clothing to conceal her ruined body. Just like a student has a thoughtless brain but steals very pleasant-sounding terms, using mask-like terms to conceal his empty brain.

This is the end of the first part of the lecture, [the relationship between current education and books].

Now comes the second part of the lecture, [the relationship between future education and movies].

The new education, the education of the scientific age, still does not exist in the world. Why is there no new education of the scientific age yet? It is because the scientific age has not yet arrived. But we are the people of the most important period in human history. What kind of period are we in? We are in the period when the religious age is beginning to prepare to transition to the scientific age. People who are now thirty to forty years old, or twenty to ten years old, are still people of the religious age, but the dawn of the scientific age is sure to come soon. Although scientific thought is very developed in America, the problem of the success of the scientific age is still not worth discussing. The education of the scientific age does not exist anywhere. We are moving towards education, experimenting, inventing, and looking for a path. It can also be said that we are creating a path because there is no prepared path. The scientific age has not yet arrived, so the education of the scientific age naturally has not yet arrived. Now it is just a hope, not something that has already been achieved.

The method of preparing for the education of the scientific age is exactly the opposite of the old method. The meaning of this scientific age is completely new: you cannot use your brain until you use your body first. Any activity must rely on the body. There cannot be internal arrangements without external stimulation.

As soon as this is said, one can understand why movies are so important in the new education of the scientific age. Movies constantly have the stimulation of things; there is never a moment without stimulation. [Without physical activity first, there cannot be brain

Page 22

activity]. This statement can be proven in tomorrow's viewing of movies. Our sound film tomorrow always has physical activity first, then speech activity. The performance of the lead actress in the movie, Mary Duncan, is very high-class. Before she speaks, she has physical activity first. For example, when she scolds men for being useless and for always bullying women, without any limits in treating women, she pushes him away. Her brain and entire body express an attitude of looking down on men. Then she says, [You are all the same.] She uses her entire body to strike first, then she utters the words to overthrow them. It can be seen in the movie how these words come out from the body. Very few actors in the film industry are able to use this kind of performance. Her words clearly come out from her physical activity. Also, when she is on the boat, her body is close to Alleen Sohn when she says, "I should make you happy, happier than any other woman ever could." The activity of her speaking posture occurs even before the sound of her voice. (To be continued)
